## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical kinetics
**Analysis**: The task models the rate of change of a chemical concentration dA_dt as a function of current concentration A and time t, which is the fundamental form of a differential rate law in reaction kinetics. The rate typically depends on the concentration of reactants, and time may appear explicitly for non-isothermal, catalytic deactivation, or complex reaction mechanisms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero‑order reaction: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, e.g., surface‑limited reactions)
- First‑order reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A (unimolecular decay, radioactive decay)
- Second‑order (single reactant): dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (dimerization or two identical reactants)
- Second‑order (two reactants): dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (reaction between two different species with initial stoichiometric imbalance)
- n‑th order reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (empirical order, power‑law kinetics)
- Reversible first‑order: dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (approach to equilibrium, isomerization)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (product‑catalyzed, logistic‑type growth, Prout–Tompkins model)
- Time‑dependent rate constant (exponential decay): dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (catalyst deactivation, radical chain termination)
- Time‑dependent rate constant (power law): dA_dt = c0 * t**c1 * A**c2 (empirical observed kinetics with changing mechanism)
- Substrate‑inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2) (enzyme kinetics with excess substrate inhibition)
- Langmuir‑Hinshelwood unimolecular: dA_dt = c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A)**2 (surface catalytic reaction with dissociative adsorption)
- Avrami–Erofeev (solid‑state): dA_dt = c0 * (1 - A) * (-c1 * log(1 - A))**c2 (nucleation and growth kinetics, for A being extent of conversion)
- Consecutive first‑order (A→B→C) with rapid equilibrium: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * (c2 - A) (coupled differential form simplified)
- Diffusion‑limited kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (c1 < 1, often 0.5, for diffusion‑controlled reactions)
- Sigmoidal solid‑state: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * (1 - A)**c2 (extended Prout–Tompkins, flexible sigmoid)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Constant rate irrespective of concentration → additive constant term (zero‑order kinetics, surface saturation)
- Rate directly proportional to concentration → term c0 * A (first‑order, exponential decay)
- Rate proportional to square of concentration → A**2 term (second‑order, dimerization) or A*(c - A) (two different reactants)
- Rate exhibits maximum then decays → product form A*(c - A) (autocatalytic, logistic‑type dynamics)
- Rate saturates at high concentration → rational fraction A/(c + A) (Michaelis‑Menten‑like enzyme saturation)
- Rate approaches zero at a non‑zero equilibrium concentration → linear term c0 - c1*A (reversible first‑order approach to equilibrium)
- Rate depends explicitly on time with power‑law or exponential decay → multiplicative factor t**c or exp(c * t) (catalyst aging, non‑isothermal effects)
- Rate limited by nucleation/growth in solid phase → terms involving log(1 - A) or (1 - A)**m (Avrami, shrinking core models)
- Rate decreased at high concentration (substrate inhibition) → denominator quadratic or higher‑order polynomial (1 + c1*A + c2*A**2)
- Rate shows fractional order <1 → power law A**c with c < 1 (diffusion‑controlled, fractal‑like kinetics)
